line=310 tag=L:             b.    * Purlka-jarra ka-pala-nyanu         nya-nyi
line=311 tag=G:                     old.man-DUAL PRESIMPF-3DUAL-REFLEX see-NPAST
line=312 tag=B:
line=313 tag=M:     2
line=314 tag=M:         The reflexive/reciprocal agreement clitic -nyanu is used in (4b) to force the coreferent interpretation.
line=315 tag=B:
line=316 tag=M:  If the clitic is replaced by the 3rd dual ob ject agreement clitic -jana , the sentence remains ungrammatical
line=317 tag=B:
line=318 tag=M:  on the coreferent interpretation, but becomes grammatical on a non-coreferent interpretation. As is, (4b) is
line=319 tag=B:
line=320 tag=M:  grammatical on the irrelevant interpretation whereby purlka-jarra "two old men" is a secondary predicate
line=321 tag=B:
line=322 tag=M:  rather than the ob ject­"They (two) see each other as two old men", cf (3b) above.
line=323 tag=B:
line=324 tag=B:
line=325 tag=B:
line=326 tag=M:                                                         7
line=327 tag=B:
line=328 tag=T+AC:                     "Theyi (two) are looking at the old meni ." (Legate 2002b)

doc_id=201 igt_id=igt201-12 1033 1056 L G L G B B B M M M M M M M M M M B M B B B T+CN T+CN+AL
language: Warlpiri (wbp)
line=1033 tag=L:  (39) Maliki-rli kaji-ngki yarlki-rni nyuntu
line=1034 tag=G:       [dog-ERG ST-3SG.2SG bite-NPST you]
line=1035 tag=L:       ngula-ju kapi-rna luwa-rni ngajulu-rlu.
line=1036 tag=G:       DEM-TOP FUT-1SG.3SG shoot-NPST me-ERG
line=1037 tag=B:
line=1038 tag=B:
line=1039 tag=B:
line=1040 tag=M:  17
line=1041 tag=M:     Here is why. In Lewis's sphere-based system, the truth-conditions a conditional If f, y are as follows:
line=1042 tag=M:  If f, y is true at world i (according to the system of spheres $) if and only if either
line=1043 tag=M:  (1) No f-world belongs to any sphere S in $i, or
line=1044 tag=M:  (2) Some sphere S in $i does contain at least one f-world, and ffiy holds at every world in S
line=1045 tag=M:  Take f=Èthis line is longer than 1", ye=Èthis line is longer than (1+e)" (note that e is a parameter, to be replaced by
line=1046 tag=M:  its value, not quoted; hence the use of Quine's quasi-quotation marks).
line=1047 tag=M:  Let $e be the sphere than contains all the worlds in which the size of the line is smaller than (1+e)" (by assumption
line=1048 tag=M:  such a sphere exists since the similarity measure in the context of speech orders worlds by the value of e at those
line=1049 tag=M:  worlds). Clearly there are f-world in $e if e>0. In these worlds ffiy is true. Hence the conditional should be true.
line=1050 tag=B:
line=1051 tag=M:                                                                                                                   21
line=1052 tag=B:
line=1053 tag=B:
line=1054 tag=B:
line=1055 tag=T+CN:        a. Reading A. `As for the dog that bites you, I'll shoot it.' (individual-centered)
line=1056 tag=T+CN+AL:        b. Reading B. `If a dog bites you, then I'll shoot it.' (possibility-centered)

line=634 tag=M:  15
line=635 tag=M:     Except where the subject is first person singular, or the clause is imperative with a second person
line=636 tag=M:  subject, in which case the regular first or second person object forms are used, respectively.
line=637 tag=M:  16
line=638 tag=M:     Hale et al (1995) use the term `non-subject' to cover object, indirect object and some other
line=639 tag=M:  benefactive-like functions of this slot.
line=640 tag=M:  17
line=641 tag=M:     For similar examples of ergative-marked secondary predicates linked to the subject in two dialects of
line=642 tag=M:  the Western Desert language, spoken to the west and south of Warlpiri, see Marsh (1992:81) on Martu
line=643 tag=M:  Wangka and Goddard (1983:127) on Yankunytjatjara.

doc_id=2979 igt_id=igt2979-16 692 714 L B M M M M M M M M M M M B B M B M B B G+LN T M+AC
language: Warlpiri (wbp)
line=692 tag=L:   (15)     Karntawarra-rlu=rlupa-nyanu mapa-ni.
line=693 tag=B:
line=694 tag=M:  18
line=695 tag=M:     The suffix -jarra in Warlpiri is normally a dual marker, but in other languages nearby (notably
line=696 tag=M:  Pitjantjatjara, where it appears in the language name in a different orthographic guise) it has developed
line=697 tag=M:  a proprietive meaning, and according to Jane Simpson (email, 16/2/2004) it appears to be used in this
line=698 tag=M:  example with a proprietive meaning on this word.
line=699 tag=M:  19
line=700 tag=M:     Within the Australianist tradition there is some terminological variation in what to call cases that
line=701 tag=M:  span ergative and instrumental functions, and even on whether to regard them as a single case (as is
line=702 tag=M:  done in the Warlpirist tradition) or as two distinct cases (as Dixon 1972 does for Dyirbal). Our
line=703 tag=M:  preference would be to label the case `instrumental' in all cases (then noting an ergative use in
line=704 tag=M:  Warlpiri, Dyirbal etc.) but here we adhere to the Warlpirist terminology.
line=705 tag=B:
line=706 tag=B:
line=707 tag=M:                                                    12
line=708 tag=B:
line=709 tag=M:  Compromising Transitivity: the Problem of Reciprocals
line=710 tag=B:
line=711 tag=B:
line=712 tag=G+LN:  WLP       ochre-ERG=1incSu-RR               paint-PR
line=713 tag=T:            `Let's paint each other / ourselves with yellow ochre.'
line=714 tag=M+AC:            (Hale, 1959 field notes)
